B00CS65JS2|5|Daft Punk set out to make an homage to the dance music they grew up with, a sound that seems to come from somewhere near Los Angeles in the late 70s or early 80s if a couple of androids had roamed the scene way back when. If you want to know all you need to know about this album, then know that there's a big controversy in music circles because people are saying this is music \\"for their dads\\" and that they'd be embarrased to listen to anything this old-sounding (read: oldschool).<br /><br />...which hilariously ignores the fact that virtually all modern dance music is based very directly on work straight out of a continuum of dance music from the 60s to the 80s, with whole genres built around samples like remixed drumbeats from talents that backed up James Brown or synthesizers that originally accompanied Donna Summer. I hate to be that old man shaking his fist at the kids on his lawn, but this is the time for it.<br /><br />Daft Punk have made a glorious album that brings back every last bit of soul and funk and \\"GIT DOWN\\" from a bygone era. This music makes me want to rent an eye-damaging color of convertible and drive it down to the beach for a twilight dance party. This music makes me want to move, to groove, and above all to smile. Daft Punk had made a name for themselves for making low-production wonders (Homework, Human After All) and they take that to the extreme on this album, using a heavy dose of live performance from real musicians with a decidedly minimal use of electronics. It's an odd situation when having the guitarist from Chic lighting up your tracks is \\"low production\\"- and the results are all the better for it.<br /><br />There is one honest fault with the album, in that it's missing any strong female presence. Considering the massive influence women had over this era, this seems like a glaring omission. A modern music critic should also note that a lot of current dance hall tracks seriously overuse female vocals, such that when you browse most popular lists of dance tracks you're guaranteed to find syrupy-sweet female lyrics just about everywhere, and the lyrics serve absolutely no point in the actual music (when the original women of dance music were often making major social and political points, particularly in the areas of female and community empowerment). Maybe Daft Punk were making their own statement regarding this problem with modern music in their anti-use of female vocals, as they're clearly making similar points with the rest of this album regarding other excesses in current music. But the album still feels incomplete, point or not.<br /><br />This album is easily a \\"top album of the decade\\". Although what decade that is, might be up for debate. If it had included a proper female presence, Random Access Memories would be a contender for \\"THE top album of the decade\\". Really enjoyable, this is going to be a staple of my listening for a long time to come.opular lists of dance tracks you're guaranteed to find syrupy-sweet female lyrics just about everywhere, and the lyrics serve absolutely no point in the actual music (when the original women of dance music were often making major social and political points, particularly in the areas of female and community empowerment). 0930289234|4|Fascist: a reactionary or dictatorial person.<br /><br />Watchmen is well written, to make a gross understatement. It is a gritty, complete world that uses the fantastic so sparingly as to create a truly immersive story. The characters are seriously flawed, just like all of humanity, and make some very very bad choices, especially in the end.<br /><br />Using logic that dictates that the ends justify the means the characters choose who lives and who dies in order to \\"save the planet\\" from the ruin of war and intolerance. The protagonists in this story are kept secret, even until the end. You are allowed to make up your own mind about who is the most right or wrong. Nobody in this story is pure... except for the god-man. And he eventually decides the fate of the world.<br /><br />And here is where the writer, Alan Moore, shows his cards. By creating a character who \\"sees the big picture\\"; who \\"is above the pettiness of human beings\\" who can't make the tough decisions, Moore has set the stage for an inevitable conclusion: some people, alot of people, an enormous number, will have to die to save the rest of us. It doesn't matter who it is, just so long as it is a bunch of them. Them. Not us. Not me. Them.<br /><br />As storytelling goes, it is nearly without flaw. Watchmen is a seminal work in the vein of HP Lovecraft's very best. Many works will take the lead on this book for one simple reason: it is a fantasy lovefest for those who want self-righteous justice.<br /><br />But, if you're not looking at it that deeply, it is also a great escape into a sweeping mystery novel that ties up every loose string in the end.

6305079900|5|'The Terminator' is a timely reminder that, once upon a time, Arnold Schwarzenegger was *way cool*, and that James Cameron was also similarly respected ('Aliens' is still the definitive Cameron film, though). Cast to  perfection, Schwarzenegger dominates the film to such a degree that the  hero, Michael Bhen, is totally overwhelmed. It's a very 1984 film - the  action is extremely violent, the music is done with synths, and the bad guy  carries an Uzi (the 'trendy movie bad guy firearm' for much of the 80's),  but it hasn't dated too badly, as it's clear set in 1984 and works as a  period piece.<br />It's a model of how to make an action film, and how  sometimes a bigger budget and more time can make a film worse. Initially,  it sets up a complex, engaging plot in a few scenes. It then develops the  plot with the minimum of fuss, moving swiftly through a mid-section that  doesn't really pause for breath, before a striking climax and a neat,  thoughtful ending. Not a scene is wasted, and not a penny is spent  unwisely.<br />Working on a tiny, 5 million dollar budget, Cameron keeps the  effects short and sweet, and with minimal publicity and no real stars, the  film must have been an unexpected surprised for the people of  1984.<br />Schwarzenegger's salary for Terminator 2 was twice the entire  budget of this film, despite which the sequel is inferior - bigger, more  impressive to look at, but slower and clunkier, and with a horribly dull  bit in the middle that a younger Cameron would have erased.<br />All in all  this is a classic piece of US cinema, and should be in your collection.

As a way to deal with this claustrophobic surveillance, Camille escapes on breaks abroad. Challenging her father's intentions and authority. But little does she realise her father has good cause to fear for her safety. On a trip away everything changes for Camille. She not only finds herself falling in love but running from danger. Unfortunately for Camille danger and love seem to go hand in hand.<br /><br />Pawn of Innocence is a good and enjoyable read. Though the beginning was a little slow, I did not think this affected the story as I enjoyed getting to know the tenacious Camille and her family and friends. For a winter read, this is the book. Filled with wonderful locations, you can easily imagine the rich world Camille inhabits. A world which is helped along with a Sights and Sounds feature. I'd never come across this before. It was an interesting addition.
